The Second Argument and Its Answer
Sanusi presents the second argument and its standard Ash'ari response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second kalam argument for why a preponderating factor must be a cause, and the standard Ash'ari response that preponderance is simultaneous with existence.

Core Idea
Preponderance is simultaneous with existence, not a prior event.

The second argument attempts to prove that preponderance itself requires a cause, but the answer shows a fundamental flaw: preponderance is not temporally prior to existence. This lesson unpacks the logic of the argument and its refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument
Read the first part of the passage (up to 'فلا بد منه') slowly. Notice how each premise builds to the conclusion that a cause is necessary.
Look for the key terms: ترجح, مؤثر, أثر.
2
Identify the premises
The argument has three premises: (1) the possible needs preponderance to exist, (2) preponderance is an existential event with a locus, (3) it cannot be the effect, so it must be the cause. Write them down.
The conclusion is that a cause is necessary.
3
Understand the answer
Read the answer ('والجواب...'). It rejects the second premise: preponderance is simultaneous with existence, not before it. Consider why this undermines the argument.
If preponderance is not prior, it cannot be a separate event requiring a cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: أن الممكن ما لم يترجح لم يوجد وترجحه أمر حدث بعد أن لم يكن فيكون وجودياً، ولا بد له من محل، وليس هو الأثر لتأخره عن الترجيح، فيكون هو المؤثر لعدم الثالث فلا بد منه. والجواب: أن الترجح مع الوجود لا قبله، إذ لا يتصور رجحان الوجود مع كون الواقع هو العدم ولو سلم فقيام ترجح وجود الممكن أو عدمه بالمؤثر ضروري البطلان. والمذكور في كلام الإمام فكان الترجح الوجوب، وهما متلازمان بناء على أن أحد الطرفين يمتنع وقوعه مع التساوي. فكيف مع المرجوحية. فالراجح لا يكون إلا واجباً، وهذا الوجوب متقدم على الوجود، أن وجود الممكن محفوف بوجوبين سابق ولاحق. وهو سيجيء من على ما نسبة بين المؤثر والأثر، يسمى من حيث الإضافة إلى المؤثر إيجاباً، وإلى الأثر وجوباً، فمنع سبقه على الوجود وكونه وصفاً للمؤثر ليس بسديد، سيما وقد قال الإمام في المباحث المشرقية: إنه على تقدير كونه ثبوتياً. فمعنى عروضه للمؤثر أنه يصير محكوماً عليه بوجوب أن يصدر عنه ذلك الأثر.
Second: that the possible does not exist until it becomes preponderant, and its preponderance is an occurrence that comes into being after it was not, so it is existential, and it must have a locus, and it is not the effect due to its posteriority to preponderance, so it is the cause due to the lack of a third, so it is necessary. The answer: that preponderance is with existence, not before it, since preponderance of existence cannot be imagined while the actual is non-existence. And if conceded, then the subsisting of the preponderance of the possible's existence or non-existence in the cause is necessarily false. And what is mentioned in the words of al-Imam, that preponderance was obligation, and they are concurrent, based on that one of the two sides is impossible to occur with equality. So how could with preponderance? So the preponderant is nothing but necessary, and this obligation precedes existence, that the existence of the possible is encompassed by two obligations: a prior and a posterior. And it will come from on what relation between cause and effect, called from the perspective of attribution to the cause 'ijab' (necessitation) and to the effect 'wujub' (necessity). So preventing its precedence over existence and its being an attribute of the cause is not sound, especially since al-Imam said in al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya: that it is, on the assumption of it being positive. So the meaning of its occurrence to the cause is that it becomes governed by an obligation to produce that effect.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage contains the second argument for the impossibility of preponderance without a cause, its answer, and a discussion of al-Imam al-Razi's view. The argument: the possible does not exist until it acquires preponderance (tarajjuh); preponderance is an event that came to be, hence it is an existential attribute; it must have a locus; it cannot be the effect because the effect is subsequent to preponderance; so it must be the cause (mu'aththir), as there is no third option. Therefore a cause is necessary. The answer rejects the argument: preponderance occurs simultaneously with existence, not before it; you cannot conceive preponderance of existence while the actual state is non-existence. Moreover, even if you concede, the idea that preponderance subsists in the cause is obviously false. The author then mentions al-Imam's view: preponderance is obligation (wujub), and they are concurrent. The reasoning: if one of the two sides is impossible given equality, then how with preponderance? The preponderant can only be necessary. This obligation precedes existence; the possible's existence is surrounded by two obligations – a prior and a posterior. The relation between cause and effect is called 'ijab' relative to the cause and 'wujub' relative to the effect. Thus denying that obligation precedes existence and is an attribute of the cause is unsound. Al-Imam's statement from al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya supports that on the assumption it is a positive attribute, its occurring to the cause means the cause becomes subject to an obligation to produce that effect.

Key Terms
ترجح
مؤثر
أثر
وجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Preponderance is an event that occurs before existence and thus itself needs a cause.
Correction: Preponderance is simultaneous with existence; it is not a prior separate event. The argument incorrectly assumes temporal priority.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, when does preponderance (tarajjuh) occur?
A) Before the existence of the possible
B) Simultaneously with existence
C) After existence
D) It does not occur at all

Key Takeaway
The second argument fails because preponderance is not temporally prior to existence, so it cannot be an event requiring a separate cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something you worked hard for, do you attribute it to your own effort alone, forgetting that Allah's will is simultaneous with every outcome? How can you train yourself to see His preponderance in each moment of success?
?
Consider a fear you have about the future. Are you trying to secure an outcome before it happens, as if preponderance could be earlier? What would it mean for your anxiety to live with the certainty that Allah's will is exactly concurrent with what actually occurs?
?
If all existence happens only when Allah's preponderance is with it, then nothing is ever out of His control. Is there an area of your life where you still feel you are the 'cause'? Write down one specific habit or belief you need to surrender, and make a sincere du'a to accept that His will is simultaneous.

Al-Imam's Equation: Preponderance as Obligation
Al-Imam's equation of preponderance with obligation and the explanation of ijab and wujub.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Imam al-Razi's view that preponderance is identical to obligation, and how this fits into the causal framework of ijab and wujub.

Core Idea
Preponderance is obligation; it precedes existence as a necessary attribute of the cause.

After the answer, the author discusses al-Imam's position that preponderance is not just a pre-requisite but is itself obligation (wujub). This lesson explains the reasoning behind this equation and the distinction between ijab (from the cause's perspective) and wujub (from the effect's perspective).

Guided Path
1
Read al-Imam's statement
Read the passage starting from 'والمذكور في كلام الإمام' up to the end. Notice the claim that preponderance is obligation.
Look for the terms وجوب and إيجاب.
2
Understand the reasoning
The reasoning: if equality makes both sides impossible, then with preponderance one side becomes necessary. Hence the preponderant is necessary. This necessity (wujub) is what preponderance is.
This connects to the idea of 'tarajjuh' as 'wujub'.
3
Grasp the two obligations and the relation
The existence of the possible is surrounded by two obligations: one prior (from the cause) and one posterior (from the effect). The relation between cause and effect is called ijab (from cause) and wujub (from effect).
Al-Imam argues that preventing obligation from preceding existence is unsound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: أن الممكن ما لم يترجح لم يوجد وترجحه أمر حدث بعد أن لم يكن فيكون وجودياً، ولا بد له من محل، وليس هو الأثر لتأخره عن الترجيح، فيكون هو المؤثر لعدم الثالث فلا بد منه. والجواب: أن الترجح مع الوجود لا قبله، إذ لا يتصور رجحان الوجود مع كون الواقع هو العدم ولو سلم فقيام ترجح وجود الممكن أو عدمه بالمؤثر ضروري البطلان. والمذكور في كلام الإمام فكان الترجح الوجوب، وهما متلازمان بناء على أن أحد الطرفين يمتنع وقوعه مع التساوي. فكيف مع المرجوحية. فالراجح لا يكون إلا واجباً، وهذا الوجوب متقدم على الوجود، أن وجود الممكن محفوف بوجوبين سابق ولاحق. وهو سيجيء من على ما نسبة بين المؤثر والأثر، يسمى من حيث الإضافة إلى المؤثر إيجاباً، وإلى الأثر وجوباً، فمنع سبقه على الوجود وكونه وصفاً للمؤثر ليس بسديد، سيما وقد قال الإمام في المباحث المشرقية: إنه على تقدير كونه ثبوتياً. فمعنى عروضه للمؤثر أنه يصير محكوماً عليه بوجوب أن يصدر عنه ذلك الأثر.
Second: that the possible does not exist until it becomes preponderant, and its preponderance is an occurrence that comes into being after it was not, so it is existential, and it must have a locus, and it is not the effect due to its posteriority to preponderance, so it is the cause due to the lack of a third, so it is necessary. The answer: that preponderance is with existence, not before it, since preponderance of existence cannot be imagined while the actual is non-existence. And if conceded, then the subsisting of the preponderance of the possible's existence or non-existence in the cause is necessarily false. And what is mentioned in the words of al-Imam, that preponderance was obligation, and they are concurrent, based on that one of the two sides is impossible to occur with equality. So how could with preponderance? So the preponderant is nothing but necessary, and this obligation precedes existence, that the existence of the possible is encompassed by two obligations: a prior and a posterior. And it will come from on what relation between cause and effect, called from the perspective of attribution to the cause 'ijab' (necessitation) and to the effect 'wujub' (necessity). So preventing its precedence over existence and its being an attribute of the cause is not sound, especially since al-Imam said in al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya: that it is, on the assumption of it being positive. So the meaning of its occurrence to the cause is that it becomes governed by an obligation to produce that effect.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage contains the second argument for the impossibility of preponderance without a cause, its answer, and a discussion of al-Imam al-Razi's view. The argument: the possible does not exist until it acquires preponderance (tarajjuh); preponderance is an event that came to be, hence it is an existential attribute; it must have a locus; it cannot be the effect because the effect is subsequent to preponderance; so it must be the cause (mu'aththir), as there is no third option. Therefore a cause is necessary. The answer rejects the argument: preponderance occurs simultaneously with existence, not before it; you cannot conceive preponderance of existence while the actual state is non-existence. Moreover, even if you concede, the idea that preponderance subsists in the cause is obviously false. The author then mentions al-Imam's view: preponderance is obligation (wujub), and they are concurrent. The reasoning: if one of the two sides is impossible given equality, then how with preponderance? The preponderant can only be necessary. This obligation precedes existence; the possible's existence is surrounded by two obligations – a prior and a posterior. The relation between cause and effect is called 'ijab' relative to the cause and 'wujub' relative to the effect. Thus denying that obligation precedes existence and is an attribute of the cause is unsound. Al-Imam's statement from al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya supports that on the assumption it is a positive attribute, its occurring to the cause means the cause becomes subject to an obligation to produce that effect.

Key Terms
وجوب
إيجاب
ترجح
مؤثر
أثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Obligation (wujub) is a temporal event that occurs before existence.
Correction: Obligation is an attribute of the cause, not a temporal event. It is a necessary relation, not something that happens in time.

Checkpoint
According to al-Imam, what is preponderance (tarajjuh)?
A) A separate event
B) An attribute of the effect
C) Obligation (wujub)
D) The cause itself

Key Takeaway
Al-Imam equates preponderance with obligation, and explains that the same relation is called ijab from the cause and wujub from the effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that 'preponderance is obligation', do you feel a tension between God's absolute freedom and the necessity implied in His causing? How does this equation affect your trust in His wisdom and justice?
?
If the cause 'becomes governed by an obligation to produce that effect', what does that mean for your understanding of God's attributes? Does it make you see His actions as more determined or more reliable? How should this shape your reliance on His promises?
?
The passage speaks of two obligations surrounding existence—prior and posterior. Reflect on your own existence: do you sense a prior obligation from your Creator that brought you into being, and a posterior obligation that now binds you to Him? How does this double necessity call you to account today?

First Objection: Creating the Existent
First objection and its refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first objection that a cause would create an already existent thing, and its refutation.

Core Idea
Creation accompanies existence in time, not before it.

The deniers argue that if a cause produces an effect at the moment the effect already exists, it would be creating the existent, which is impossible. Al-Isfarayini responds by clarifying that creation accompanies existence in time, and this does not imply essential posteriority.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the first objection carefully: it claims that if a cause acts when the effect exists, it is creating the existent; if when the effect is non-existent, it combines contradictories.
The objection uses the concept of 'ījād al-mawjūd' (creating the existent) as an impossibility.
2
Identify the refutation
The refutation states that the impossible is creating an existent with an existence other than the act of creation. What actually happens is that existence accompanies creation in time.
Key phrase: 'al-wujūd yuqārin al-ījād bi al-zamān' (existence accompanies creation in time).
3
Understand the nuance
Notice that this response distinguishes between temporal accompaniment and essential priority. The cause is prior in essence, not necessarily in time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبه المنكرين على عدم الاحتياج . قال : ومن أقوى شبه المنكرين . أن التأخير حال الوجود، إيجاد للموجود، وحال العدم جمع بين النقيضين وأن الضرورة قاضية بوقع الترجيح بلا مرجح في مثل الهارب من السبع يسلك أحد الطريقين، والعطشان يشرب أحد الماءين مع التساوي، وأن العدم نفي محض لا يصلح أثراً . والجواب عن الأول : أن المحال إيجاد الموجود بوجود حاصل، بغير هذا الإيجاد، وهو غير لازم غايته أن الوجود يقارن الإيجاد بالزمان، وهو لا ينافي التأخر بالذات . وعن الثاني: أن اللازم على تقدير التسليم ترجيح المختار أحد المتساويين، بلا مخصص لا الترجح بلا سبب . فإن قيل : هذا الاختيار والترجيح وقع بلا سبب. قلنا : ممنوع بل الإرادة التي من شأنها الترجيح والتخصيص. وعن الثالث: أنه عدم مضاف مستند إلى عدم العلة . بمعنى أن العقل يحكم بأنه عدم لعدم علته، وأما التمسك بأن العلية لكونها نقيض اللاعلية ثبوتية. وكذا موصوفها، وبأن التأثير إما في الماهية، أو الوجود، أو الموصوفية ، والكل باطل لما سبق ، وبأنه لو وجدت المؤثر به أو الحاجة تسلسلت فضعفه ظاهر .
The objections of the deniers against the need for a cause. He said: Among the strongest objections of the deniers are: That delaying at the time of existence is creating the existent, and at the time of non-existence is combining the two contradictories; and that necessity judges the occurrence of preference without a preferrer, like the one fleeing from a beast who takes one of two paths, and the thirsty one who drinks one of two waters while they are equal; and that non-existence is pure negation and is not fit to be an effect. The answer to the first: That the impossible is creating the existent with an existing existence other than this creation, and this is not necessary; at most, existence accompanies creation in time, and this does not contradict essential posteriority. The answer to the second: That the necessary, on the assumption of the admission, is the preferrer's preference of one of two equals without a specifier, not the preference without a cause. If it is said: This choice and preference occurred without a cause. We say: It is denied; rather, it is the will whose attribute is preference and specification. The answer to the third: That it is a relative non-existence based on the non-existence of the cause, meaning that the intellect judges that it is non-existence due to the non-existence of its cause. As for clinging to the fact that causality, because it is the opposite of non-causality, is positive, and likewise its subject; and that the effect is either in the essence, or existence, or description, and all are invalid due to what preceded; and that if there were an effecter or need, they would regress, so its weakness is apparent.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage presents three objections made by deniers (al-munkirīn) against the claim that a contingent being (mumkin) requires a cause for its existence. The first objection: if a cause were to produce an effect at the moment the effect already exists, that would be creating an already existent thing (ījād al-mawjūd), which is impossible. If it were to produce it at the moment of non-existence, that would be combining the contradictory states of existence and non-existence. The second objection: ordinary experience shows that a person fleeing a beast may choose one of two equivalent paths without any preferrer, and a thirsty person may drink one of two equal cups of water, indicating that preference can occur without a cause. The third objection: non-existence is pure negation and thus cannot serve as an effect. The responses are then given. To the first, the author replies that the impossibility is in creating an existent with an existence separate from the act of creation; but if creation accompanies existence in time, that does not entail essential posteriority. To the second, he argues that what actually occurs is the preferrer's preference of one of the two equals by a specifier, not preference without a cause; if one objects that the will itself is uncaused, the author says this is denied, for the will is by nature a specifier. To the third, he explains that non-existence is relative to the absence of a cause, so it is not an absolute effect; the arguments based on causality being positive, etc., are invalid for reasons already given, and positing a self-sufficient regress is impossible.

Key Terms
إيجاد الموجود
جمع بين النقيضين
تأخر بالذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That if a cause acts when the effect already exists, it would be redundant and impossible.
Correction: Creation accompanies existence in time, so there is no redundancy; the cause is prior in essence.

Checkpoint
What is the refutation's key point regarding the first objection?
A) The cause must be prior in time.
B) Existence accompanies creation in time, not essential priority.
C) The objection is valid and accepted.
D) The effect exists before the cause.

Key Takeaway
The first objection fails because creation does not require temporal priority; existence accompanies creation in time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the fact that Allah's act of creation is not bound by time, how does that change the way you think about His power in your own life? Are there situations where you have been impatient, expecting God to act according to your timeline?
?
If existence accompanies creation and does not require a prior moment of non-existence, what does that mean for your understanding of God's constant maintenance of the universe? Do you live as if everything depends on Him every moment?
?
The objection assumes that creation must fit into our human concept of time. Where in your life have you placed God's actions into a temporal box, expecting Him to follow your sequence of events? Will you surrender that expectation today?

Second Objection: Preference Without a Preferrer
Second objection and its refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection that preference can occur without a cause, and its refutation.

Core Idea
Choice is always caused by a will that specifies.

The denizens argue that ordinary experience shows people choosing between equivalent options without any preferrer, implying that preference can occur without a cause. Al-Isfarayini responds by arguing that what actually happens is the preferrer's choice by a specifier, and the will itself is that specifier.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The objection uses examples of a person fleeing from a beast choosing one of two equal paths, or a thirsty person choosing one of two equal cups of water. This supposedly shows preference without a cause.
Key phrase: 'tarjīḥ bilā murajjiḥ' (preference without a preferrer).
2
Understand the refutation's premise
The refutation distinguishes between the preferrer's preference (tarjīḥ al-mukhtār) and preference without a cause. The former requires a specifier.
Al-Isfarayini says: 'al-lāzim ʿalā taqdīr al-taslīm tarjīḥ al-mukhtār aḥad al-mutasāwiyayn, bilā mukhaṣṣiṣ' (the necessary, on the assumption of admission, is the preferrer's preference of one of two equals without a specifier).
3
Identify the answer to the follow-up objection
If one asks where the specifier comes from, the answer is that the will (irāda) itself is the specifier by nature.
Key term: 'al-irāda allatī min shaʾnihā al-tarjīḥ wa al-takhṣīṣ' (the will whose attribute is preference and specification).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبه المنكرين على عدم الاحتياج . قال : ومن أقوى شبه المنكرين . أن التأخير حال الوجود، إيجاد للموجود، وحال العدم جمع بين النقيضين وأن الضرورة قاضية بوقع الترجيح بلا مرجح في مثل الهارب من السبع يسلك أحد الطريقين، والعطشان يشرب أحد الماءين مع التساوي، وأن العدم نفي محض لا يصلح أثراً . والجواب عن الأول : أن المحال إيجاد الموجود بوجود حاصل، بغير هذا الإيجاد، وهو غير لازم غايته أن الوجود يقارن الإيجاد بالزمان، وهو لا ينافي التأخر بالذات . وعن الثاني: أن اللازم على تقدير التسليم ترجيح المختار أحد المتساويين، بلا مخصص لا الترجح بلا سبب . فإن قيل : هذا الاختيار والترجيح وقع بلا سبب. قلنا : ممنوع بل الإرادة التي من شأنها الترجيح والتخصيص. وعن الثالث: أنه عدم مضاف مستند إلى عدم العلة . بمعنى أن العقل يحكم بأنه عدم لعدم علته، وأما التمسك بأن العلية لكونها نقيض اللاعلية ثبوتية. وكذا موصوفها، وبأن التأثير إما في الماهية، أو الوجود، أو الموصوفية ، والكل باطل لما سبق ، وبأنه لو وجدت المؤثر به أو الحاجة تسلسلت فضعفه ظاهر .
The objections of the deniers against the need for a cause. He said: Among the strongest objections of the deniers are: That delaying at the time of existence is creating the existent, and at the time of non-existence is combining the two contradictories; and that necessity judges the occurrence of preference without a preferrer, like the one fleeing from a beast who takes one of two paths, and the thirsty one who drinks one of two waters while they are equal; and that non-existence is pure negation and is not fit to be an effect. The answer to the first: That the impossible is creating the existent with an existing existence other than this creation, and this is not necessary; at most, existence accompanies creation in time, and this does not contradict essential posteriority. The answer to the second: That the necessary, on the assumption of the admission, is the preferrer's preference of one of two equals without a specifier, not the preference without a cause. If it is said: This choice and preference occurred without a cause. We say: It is denied; rather, it is the will whose attribute is preference and specification. The answer to the third: That it is a relative non-existence based on the non-existence of the cause, meaning that the intellect judges that it is non-existence due to the non-existence of its cause. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does realizing that your will is a specifier change how you see the responsibility for that choice? Commit now to reflect before future decisions: 'My will is not uncaused; I am accountable for what it specifies.'
?
You often attribute your choices to 'no reason' or 'just because.' But this lesson says your will is always the cause. What does that reveal about your heart's preferences? Ask yourself: 'What does my will naturally lean toward when no external pressure is present? Is that leaning pleasing to Allah?' Write down one area where you need to retrain your will.
?

Now apply that to yourself: when you sin, do you hide behind 'I didn't mean to' or 'it just happened'? Confront the truth: your will was involved. What will you do tomorrow to align your will with obedience?

Third Objection: Non-Existence as an Effect
Third objection and its refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third objection that non-existence cannot be an effect, and its refutation.

Core Idea
Non-existence is relative to absence of a cause, not an absolute effect.

The deniers argue that non-existence is pure negation and thus cannot be an effect of a cause. Al-Isfarayini responds by explaining that non-existence is relative (ʿadam muḍāf) based on the absence of a cause, and that the arguments claiming causality is positive are invalid.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The objection states that non-existence (ʿadam) is pure negation and therefore cannot serve as an effect.
Key phrase: 'al-ʿadam nafy maḥḍ lā yaṣluḥ atharan' (non-existence is pure negation and is not fit to be an effect).
2
Understand the refutation's core idea
The refutation defines non-existence as relative (ʿadam muḍāf) based on the non-existence of the cause. The intellect judges that something is non-existent due to the absence of its cause.
Key term: 'ʿadam muḍāf' (relative non-existence).
3
Note the additional arguments
Al-Isfarayini dismisses arguments that causality is positive, that the effect is in essence, existence, or description, and that an infinite regress would occur. He says their weakness is apparent.
These are brief and rely on previous discussions ('limā sabaqa').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The objections of the deniers against the need for a cause. He said: Among the strongest objections of the deniers are: That delaying at the time of existence is creating the existent, and at the time of non-existence is combining the two contradictories; and that necessity judges the occurrence of preference without a preferrer, like the one fleeing from a beast who takes one of two paths, and the thirsty one who drinks one of two waters while they are equal; and that non-existence is pure negation and is not fit to be an effect. The answer to the first: That the impossible is creating the existent with an existing existence other than this creation, and this is not necessary; at most, existence accompanies creation in time, and this does not contradict essential posteriority. The answer to the second: That the necessary, on the assumption of the admission, is the preferrer's preference of one of two equals without a specifier, not the preference without a cause. If it is said: This choice and preference occurred without a cause. We say: It is denied; rather, it is the will whose attribute is preference and specification. The answer to the third: That it is a relative non-existence based on the non-existence of the cause, meaning that the intellect judges that it is non-existence due to the non-existence of its cause. As for clinging to the fact that causality, because it is the opposite of non-causality, is positive, and likewise its subject; and that the effect is either in the essence, or existence, or description, and all are invalid due to what preceded; and that if there were an effecter or need, they would regress, so its weakness is apparent.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage presents three objections made by deniers (al-munkirīn) against the claim that a contingent being (mumkin) requires a cause for its existence. The first objection: if a cause were to produce an effect at the moment the effect already exists, that would be creating an already existent thing (ījād al-mawjūd), which is impossible. If it were to produce it at the moment of non-existence, that would be combining the contradictory states of existence and non-existence. The second objection: ordinary experience shows that a person fleeing a beast may choose one of two equivalent paths without any preferrer, and a thirsty person may drink one of two equal cups of water, indicating that preference can occur without a cause. The third objection: non-existence is pure negation and thus cannot serve as an effect. The responses are then given. To the first, the author replies that the impossibility is in creating an existent with an existence separate from the act of creation; but if creation accompanies existence in time, that does not entail essential posteriority. To the second, he argues that what actually occurs is the preferrer's preference of one of the two equals by a specifier, not preference without a cause; if one objects that the will itself is uncaused, the author says this is denied, for the will is by nature a specifier. To the third, he explains that non-existence is relative to the absence of a cause, so it is not an absolute effect; the arguments based on causality being positive, etc., are invalid for reasons already given, and positing a self-sufficient regress is impossible.

Key Terms
عدم نفي محض
عدم مضاف
علة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That non-existence can be a direct effect of a cause.
Correction: Non-existence is relative to the absence of a cause, not an effect produced by a cause.

Checkpoint
How does Al-Isfarayini define non-existence in his refutation?
A) As pure negation with no relation to a cause.
B) As relative non-existence based on the absence of a cause.
C) As an effect produced by a cause.
D) As a positive attribute.

Key Takeaway
The third objection fails because non-existence is relative to the absence of a cause, not an effect in itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of something that does not exist in your life—whether a blessing you lack or a trial you fear—do you see it as an absolute nothing, or do you recognize its non-existence as tied to the absence of a cause? How does this perspective shift your reliance on Allāh as the sole Creator of causes?
?
Consider a moment you felt Allah had withheld something from you. Did you attribute that 'not having' to His wisdom or to mere chance? This lesson teaches that non-existence is relative and caused. How does knowing that even your 'lacks' are under His control change how you respond to them today?
?
You often thank Allāh for what exists. But do you realize that the non-existence of harm or difficulty is also an effect of His mercy—tied to the absence of its cause? What specific non-existence (e.g., health, safety) have you taken for granted as simply 'not there' rather than as a created effect of His protection? Make a concrete intention to acknowledge this in your next du'ā.

The Deniers' Dilemma on Causality and Its Critique
Al-Isfarayini presents the deniers' dilemma and begins his critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the deniers' argument that an effecter's action is impossible at both existence and non-existence, and the author's initial critique of the claim that non-existence is continuous.

Core Idea
The deniers' dilemma is a flawed attempt to deny causality, because non-existence can be temporal.

This passage presents an argument from deniers of causality, who claim that an effecter cannot act either when the effect exists (redundant) or when it does not (contradictory). The author critiques this, especially the claim that non-existence is continuous, pointing out that non-existence can be temporal. This lesson unpacks the dilemma and the beginning of the rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Identify the main argument attributed to the deniers.
Notice the reference to Democritus and the heavens existing by chance.
2
Analyze the dilemma
The deniers argue that an effecter's action must occur either when the effect exists or when it does not. Understand why each option is deemed invalid.
Existence case: effect would be redundant. Non-existence case: contradictory combination of existence and non-existence.
3
Focus on the author's critique
The author challenges the third reason from al-Mawaqif that non-existence is continuous. Why does he say it is not complete?
Non-existence can be temporal (حادثاً لا مستمراً). This undermines the claim that it cannot be an effect.
4
Reflect on the significance
Think about why this critique matters for the overall discussion of causality. The deniers' argument is weakened if non-existence is not always continuous.
This opens the door for a more nuanced understanding of causal influence.

ذكر الإمام من جانب المنكرين لامتناع وقوع الممكن بلا سبب كديمقراطيس وأتباعه القائلين : بأن وجود السموات بطريق الاتفاق، شبهاً ، منها، أنه لو احتاج المسكن إلى مؤثر فتأثيره فيه إما أن يكون حال وجوده ، وهو إيجاب للموجود، وتحصيل للحاصل، أو حال عدمه، وهو جمع بين النقيضين، أعني العدم الذي كان والوجود الذي حصل، وما ذكر في المواقف من أن كون التأثير حال العدم باطل، لأنه جمع بين النقيضين، ولأن العدم نفي صرف فلا يصلح أثراً ، ولأنه مستمر، فلا يستند إلى مؤثر الوجود، ليس على ما ينبغي، لأن الكلام في التأثير بمعنى الإيجاد، وإلا لما صح أن التأثير حال الوجود إيجاد الموجود، وحال العدم جمع النقيضين، على أن الوجه الثالث ليس بتام، لأن العدم ربما يكون حادثاً لا مستمراً، لا يقال في الكلام اختصار. والمراد أن التأثير أعم من الإيجاد والإعدام، أما حال الوجود وهو باطل، لأنه إيجاد الموجود ، ولأن العدم نفي محض ، وأما حال العدم، وهو باطل، لأنه النقيضين، ولأن العدم نفي محض، لأنا نقول لو أريد ذلك لم يكن لقوله ، فلا يستند معنى الوجود إلى مؤثر ، لأن العدم على تقديد كونه أثراً، إنما يستند إلى مؤثر العدم لا الوجود. وبهذا تبين، أن ليس قوله. ولأنه نفي محض، أو قوله : ولأنه مستمر ابتداء شبهة على نفي التأثير بمعنى أن الممكن لو احتاج إلى مؤثر في وجوده، لاحتاج إليه في عدمه، وهو باطل، لأنه نفي محض، ولأنه مستمر. كيف وقد أورد بعد ذلك هذه الشبهة بعينها، والمذكور في كلام الإمام أن التأثير حال العدم باطل، لأنه لا أثر حينئذ، فلا تأثير، لأنه إما عين الأثر ، أو ملزومه، بناء على أن كون المعلول متأخراً عن العلة بحسب الزمان . العلة، جمع والجواب : أنا نختار أن التأثير حال الوجود فإن أريد بإيجاد الموجود
The Imam mentioned from the side of the deniers of the impossibility of a contingent occurrence without a cause, like Democritus and his followers who say that the existence of the heavens is by coincidence, [giving] arguments, including: that if the effect needed an effecter, its effect in it would either be at the time of its existence—which is confirming the existent and obtaining the obtained—or at the time of its non-existence—which is combining the two contradictories, i.e., the non-existence that was and the existence that occurred. And what was mentioned in al-Mawaqif, that the effect being at the time of non-existence is invalid because it is combining the two contradictories, and because non-existence is pure negation so it is not fit to be an effect, and because it is continuous so it is not based on an effecter of existence, is not as it should be, because the discussion is about effect in the sense of bringing into existence, otherwise it would not be correct that the effect at the time of existence is creating the existent, and at the time of non-existence is combining the contradictories. However, the third aspect is not complete, because non-existence might be temporal not continuous. It is not said that the speech is abbreviated. The intended meaning is that effect is more general than bringing into existence and annihilating. As for at the time of existence, it is invalid because it is creating the existent, and because non-existence is pure negation. As for at the time of non-existence, it is invalid because it is the two contradictories, and because non-existence is pure negation. For we say: if that were intended, his statement would not be: 'so it is not based on a meaning of existence with an effecter', because non-existence, even if considered an effect, is only based on an effecter of non-existence, not of existence. And with this it is clear that his statement 'because it is pure negation' or his statement 'because it is continuous' is not a beginning of an objection against the denial of effect in the sense that if the contingent needed an effecter in its existence, it would need it in its non-existence, and that is invalid because it is pure negation and because it is continuous. How indeed he later mentioned this very objection? And what is mentioned in the Imam's speech is that the effect at the time of non-existence is invalid because there is no effect then, so there is no effect, because it is either the essence of the effect or its concomitant, based on the fact that the effect is posterior to the cause in time. The cause, plural. And the answer: we choose that the effect is at the time of existence. If it is intended by 'creating the existent'...
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the deniers' arguments against the need for a cause. It specifically references Democritus and his followers, who hold that the heavens exist by chance. The argument recapitulates the dilemma: an effecter's action on the effect is either at the time of existence (which is creating the existent) or at the time of non-existence (which is combining contradictories). The author then critiques the treatment of this argument in al-Mawaqif, noting that the third aspect (non-existence as continuous) is not complete because non-existence can be temporal. He clarifies that 'effect' (ta'thīr) is more general than 'bringing into existence' (ījād) and 'annihilating' (i'dām). The passage then delves into a detailed rebuttal, arguing that non-existence, even if considered an effect, is attributed to an effecter of non-existence, not existence. The author points out a flaw in the opponent's reasoning and then presents the answer chosen by the authorial position: that the effect occurs at the time of existence. However, the text cuts off mid-sentence at 'if it is intended by creating the existent...', so the full response is not preserved in this window.

D) Because the argument is taken from al-Mawaqif and is correct.

Key Takeaway
The deniers' argument fails because it wrongly assumes non-existence is always continuous, while it can be temporal.

?

The Objection Against Causal Influence: The Dilemma of Timing
The author presents and critiques an objection against causal influence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that if the contingent needed a cause, the cause's influence would have to occur either when the effect already exists (making it redundant) or when it does not (making it contradictory).

Core Idea
If the contingent needs a cause, the cause's influence is either redundant or impossible.

This passage presents an objection from those who deny the need for a cause, like Democritus. They argue that if the contingent required a cause, the cause's influence would have to occur either when the effect already exists (making it redundant) or when it does not (which is contradictory). The author then critiques a previous formulation of this objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice the two options presented: influence at existence or at non-existence.
2
Understand the two horns
Identify why each option is considered problematic: at existence it is tautological, at non-existence it is contradictory.
The phrase 'جمع بين النقيضين' means 'combining opposites'.
3
Examine the critique of al-Mawaqif
The author notes that the formulation in al-Mawaqif is not accurate because it assumes influence at non-existence is false for three reasons, but the author questions this.
The author points out that non-existence can be temporal, not always perpetual.
4
Reflect on the challenge
Consider why this objection is serious for those who affirm causation in contingent beings.
This sets the stage for the author's refutation in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكر الإمام من جانب المنكرين لامتناع وقوع الممكن بلا سبب كديمقراطيس وأتباعه القائلين : بأن وجود السموات بطريق الاتفاق، شبهة منها، أنه لو احتاج الممكن إلى مؤثر فتأثيره فيه إما أن يكون حال وجوده ، وهو إيجاب للموجود، وتحصيل للحاصل، أو حال عدمه، وهو جمع بين النقيضين، أعني العدم الذي كان والوجود الذي حصل، وما ذكر في المواقف من أن كون التأثير حال العدم باطل، لأنه جمع بين النقيضين، ولأن العدم نفي صرف فلا يصلح أثراً ، ولأنه مستمر، فلا يستند إلى مؤثر الوجود، ليس على ما ينبغي، لأن الكلام في التأثير بمعنى الإيجاد، وإلا لما صح أن التأثير حال الوجود إيجاد الموجود، وحال العدم جمع النقيضين، على أن الوجه تبين، أن ليس قوله. ولأنه نفي محض، أو قوله : ولأنه مستمر ابتداء شبهة على نفي التأثير بمعنى أن الممكن لو احتاج إلى مؤثر في وجوده، لاحتاج إليه في عدمه، وهو باطل، لأنه نفي محض، ولأنه مستمر. كيف وقد أورد بعد ذلك هذه الشبهة بعينها، والمذكور في كلام الإمام أن التأثير حال العدم باطل، لأنه لا أثر حينئذ، فلا تأثير، لأنه إما عين الأثر، أو ملزومه، بناء على أن كون المعلول متأخراً عن العلة بحسب الزمان . والجواب : أنا نختار أن التأثير حال الوجود فإن أريد بإيجاد الموجود الموجود بالوجود الحاصل بهذا الإيجاد، فلا نسلم استحالته، القابل. فإن السواد قائم بالجسم الأسود بهذا السواد، وإن أريد بوجود آخر سابق فلا نسلم لزومه فإن الوجود الحاصل بالتأثير مقارن له. وقد نختار أن التأثير حال العدم، ولا جمع بين النقيضين، لأن الأثر عقيب التأثير، بناء على أن المؤثر سابق على الأثر بالزمان أيضاً، ومعنى امتناع التخلف أنه لا يتخللهما آن وكان هذا مراد من أجاب بأن وجود المؤثر يستتبع وجود الأثر، على معنى أن وجود الأثر يحصل عقيب وجود المؤثر بصفة المؤثرية، وهو معنى التأثير فيكون في أن عدم الأثر، ويكون معنى تأثيره في الممكن إخراجه من العدم إلى الوجود
The Imam mentioned on behalf of the deniers of the impossibility of the occurrence of the contingent without a cause, like Democritus and his followers who say that the existence of the heavens is by chance, an objection from them: that if the contingent needed an efficient cause, then its influence upon it would either be at the time of its existence, which is making what exists exist and obtaining what is obtained, or at the time of its non-existence, which is combining the two opposites, namely the non-existence that was and the existence that occurred. And what was mentioned in al-Mawaqif that the influence being at the time of non-existence is false because it combines two opposites, and because non-existence is pure negation so it is not suitable as an effect, and because it is perpetual so it does not depend on a cause of existence, is not as it should be, because the discussion is about influence in the sense of bringing into existence; otherwise it would not be correct that influence at the time of existence is making what exists exist, and at the time of non-existence is combining two opposites. Moreover, the third aspect is not complete, because non-existence may be temporal not perpetual. It is not said that in the argument there is abbreviation. The intended meaning is that influence is more general than bringing into existence and annihilating. As for the state of existence, it is false because it is making what exists exist, and because non-existence is pure negation. As for the state of non-existence, it is false because it combines two opposites, and because non-existence is pure negation. For we say: if that were intended, his statement would not be: 'so it does not depend on a cause of existence', because non-existence, if considered as an effect, only depends on a cause of non-existence, not existence. And by this it is clear that his statement 'because it is pure negation' or his statement 'because it is perpetual' is not the beginning of an objection against negation of influence in the sense that if the contingent needed a cause for its existence, it would need it for its non-existence, and it is false because it is pure negation and because it is perpetual. How can it be, when he later mentioned this same objection? And what is mentioned in the Imam's speech that influence at the time of non-existence is false because there is no effect then, so no influence, because it is either the very effect or its necessary condition, based on the effect being temporally posterior to the cause. The answer: We choose that influence is at the time of existence. If by 'making what exists exist' is meant the existence obtained by this act of bringing into existence, we do not admit its impossibility; for blackness subsists in the black body by this blackness. And if another prior existence is meant, we do not admit its entailment, for the existence obtained by the influence is simultaneous with it. And we may choose that influence is at the time of non-existence, and there is no combining of opposites, because the effect is immediately after the influence, based on the cause being temporally prior to the effect as well. The meaning of the impossibility of delay is that no moment intervenes between them. And this was the intention of the one who answered that the existence of the cause entails the existence of the effect, meaning that the existence of the effect occurs immediately after the existence of the cause with the quality of being a cause, which is the meaning of influence, so it is as if it is the non-existence of the effect, and the meaning of its influence on the contingent is bringing it out from non-existence to existence.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes an objection against the necessity of a cause for contingent existence. The objectors, like Democritus, argue that if a contingent needs a cause, the cause's influence must occur either when the effect already exists (resulting in tautology) or when it does not exist (combining opposites). The author critiques a formulation in al-Mawaqif, clarifying that 'influence' here means 'bringing into existence'. He then provides two possible answers: (1) influence at the time of existence is acceptable if the existence obtained is the very existence resulting from that influence, not a prior one; (2) influence at the time of non-existence is also possible if the effect follows immediately, with no temporal gap. This refutes the objection that influence is impossible.

حال العدم
إيجاد الموجود
جمع النقيضين

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that influence at non-existence is always impossible because non-existence is pure negation and perpetual.
Correction: The author clarifies that non-existence can be temporal, and influence at non-existence can be meaningful if the effect follows immediately.

Checkpoint
According to the objection, why is influence at the time of existence considered problematic?
A) It combines opposites
B) It makes what already exists exist (tautology)
C) It requires a temporal gap
D) It is not a real cause

Key Takeaway
The objection claims that causal influence is impossible because it must occur either when the effect exists (redundant) or when it does not (contradictory).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does the logical necessity of a cause for every contingent being challenge the sense of purposelessness you might sometimes feel? Will you sit with this truth until it transforms how you see your own life?
?
The objectors argue that a cause is either redundant or contradictory. Have you ever used similar reasoning to avoid acknowledging a higher purpose or accountability in your life—perhaps by thinking that your actions don't matter or that God's creation is impossible? What would it cost you to truly accept that your existence demands a cause beyond yourself?
?
If the influence at non-existence is not a contradiction but the very act of creation, how does that reshape your trust in God's power to bring things from nothing? Do you live as if you are self-sufficient, or do you constantly recognize that you are sustained moment by moment? What would change today if you deeply internalized that you are not self-caused?

Refuting the Objection: Two Viable Alternatives
The author refutes the objection by presenting two viable alternatives for causal influence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the objection by showing that influence can occur at existence (as simultaneous creation) or at non-existence (as immediate succession).

Core Idea
Causal influence can occur either at existence or non-existence without contradiction.

In this passage, the author directly answers the objection. He clarifies that influence means bringing into existence. He then presents two choices: either influence occurs at the time of existence, but the existence is the very one produced (not tautological), or influence occurs at non-existence, but the effect follows immediately with no temporal gap, avoiding contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's clarification
The author first clarifies that the discussion is about influence as bringing into existence (إيجاد).
This is crucial for understanding the answers.
2
First answer: influence at existence
If influence is at existence, the existence obtained is the one resulting from this influence, not a prior existence—so no tautology. Example: blackness subsists in a black body.
The author uses the example of blackness to show that simultaneous existence is not impossible.
3
Second answer: influence at non-existence
If influence is at non-existence, the effect occurs immediately after the influence, with no temporal gap, so there is no combining of opposites.
This is based on the cause being temporally prior to the effect.
4
Understand the concept of immediate succession
The meaning of 'impossibility of delay' is that no moment intervenes between cause and effect. Influence brings the effect from non-existence to existence.
This refutes the objection that influence at non-existence is contradictory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكر الإمام من جانب المنكرين لامتناع وقوع الممكن بلا سبب كديمقراطيس وأتباعه القائلين : بأن وجود السموات بطريق الاتفاق، شبهة منها، أنه لو احتاج الممكن إلى مؤثر فتأثيره فيه إما أن يكون حال وجوده ، وهو إيجاب للموجود، وتحصيل للحاصل، أو حال عدمه، وهو جمع بين النقيضين، أعني العدم الذي كان والوجود الذي حصل، وما ذكر في المواقف من أن كون التأثير حال العدم باطل، لأنه جمع بين النقيضين، ولأن العدم نفي صرف فلا يصلح أثراً ، ولأنه مستمر، فلا يستند إلى مؤثر الوجود، ليس على ما ينبغي، لأن الكلام في التأثير بمعنى الإيجاد، وإلا لما صح أن التأثير حال الوجود إيجاد الموجود، وحال العدم جمع النقيضين، على أن الوجه الثالث ليس بتام، لأن العدم ربما يكون حادثاً لا مستمراً، لا يقال في الكلام اختصار. والمراد أن التأثير أعم من الإيجاد والإعدام، أما حال الوجود وهو باطل، لأنه إيجاد الموجود ، ولأن العدم نفي محض، وأما حال العدم، وهو باطل، لأنه النقيضين، ولأن العدم نفي محض، لأنا نقول لو أريد ذلك لم يكن لقوله، فلا يستند معنى الوجود إلى مؤثر ، لأن العدم على تقدير كونه أثراً، إنما يستند إلى مؤثر العدم لا الوجود. وبهذا تبين، أن ليس قوله. ولأنه نفي محض، أو قوله : ولأنه مستمر ابتداء شبهة على نفي التأثير بمعنى أن الممكن لو احتاج إلى مؤثر في وجوده، لاحتاج إليه في عدمه، وهو باطل، لأنه نفي محض، ولأنه مستمر. كيف وقد أورد بعد ذلك هذه الشبهة بعينها، والمذكور في كلام الإمام أن التأثير حال العدم باطل، لأنه لا أثر حينئذ، فلا تأثير، لأنه إما عين الأثر، أو ملزومه، بناء على أن كون المعلول متأخراً عن العلة بحسب الزمان . والجواب : أنا نختار أن التأثير حال الوجود فإن أريد بإيجاد الموجود الموجود بالوجود الحاصل بهذا الإيجاد، فلا نسلم استحالته، القابل. فإن السواد قائم بالجسم الأسود بهذا السواد، وإن أريد بوجود آخر سابق فلا نسلم لزومه فإن الوجود الحاصل بالتأثير مقارن له. وقد نختار أن التأثير حال العدم، ولا جمع بين النقيضين، لأن الأثر عقيب التأثير، بناء على أن المؤثر سابق على الأثر بالزمان أيضاً، ومعنى امتناع التخلف أنه لا يتخللهما آن وكان هذا مراد من أجاب بأن وجود المؤثر يستتبع وجود الأثر، على معنى أن وجود الأثر يحصل عقيب وجود المؤثر بصفة المؤثرية، وهو معنى التأثير فيكون في أن عدم الأثر، ويكون معنى تأثيره في الممكن إخراجه من العدم إلى الوجود
The Imam mentioned on behalf of the deniers of the impossibility of the occurrence of the contingent without a cause, like Democritus and his followers who say that the existence of the heavens is by chance, an objection from them: that if the contingent needed an efficient cause, then its influence upon it would either be at the time of its existence, which is making what exists exist and obtaining what is obtained, or at the time of its non-existence, which is combining the two opposites, namely the non-existence that was and the existence that occurred. And what was mentioned in al-Mawaqif that the influence being at the time of non-existence is false because it combines two opposites, and because non-existence is pure negation so it is not suitable as an effect, and because it is perpetual so it does not depend on a cause of existence, is not as it should be, because the discussion is about influence in the sense of bringing into existence; otherwise it would not be correct that influence at the time of existence is making what exists exist, and at the time of non-existence is combining two opposites. Moreover, the third aspect is not complete, because non-existence may be temporal not perpetual. It is not said that in the argument there is abbreviation. The intended meaning is that influence is more general than bringing into existence and annihilating. As for the state of existence, it is false because it is making what exists exist, and because non-existence is pure negation. As for the state of non-existence, it is false because it combines two opposites, and because non-existence is pure negation. For we say: if that were intended, his statement would not be: 'so it does not depend on a cause of existence', because non-existence, if considered as an effect, only depends on a cause of non-existence, not existence. And by this it is clear that his statement 'because it is pure negation' or his statement 'because it is perpetual' is not the beginning of an objection against negation of influence in the sense that if the contingent needed a cause for its existence, it would need it for its non-existence, and it is false because it is pure negation and because it is perpetual. How can it be, when he later mentioned this same objection? And what is mentioned in the Imam's speech that influence at the time of non-existence is false because there is no effect then, so no influence, because it is either the very effect or its necessary condition, based on the effect being temporally posterior to the cause. The answer: We choose that influence is at the time of existence. If by 'making what exists exist' is meant the existence obtained by this act of bringing into existence, we do not admit its impossibility; for blackness subsists in the black body by this blackness. And if another prior existence is meant, we do not admit its entailment, for the existence obtained by the influence is simultaneous with it. And we may choose that influence is at the time of non-existence, and there is no combining of opposites, because the effect is immediately after the influence, based on the cause being temporally prior to the effect as well. The meaning of the impossibility of delay is that no moment intervenes between them. And this was the intention of the one who answered that the existence of the cause entails the existence of the effect, meaning that the existence of the effect occurs immediately after the existence of the cause with the quality of being a cause, which is the meaning of influence, so it is as if it is the non-existence of the effect, and the meaning of its influence on the contingent is bringing it out from non-existence to existence.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes an objection against the necessity of a cause for contingent existence. The objectors, like Democritus, argue that if a contingent needs a cause, the cause's influence must occur either when the effect already exists (resulting in tautology) or when it does not exist (combining opposites). The author critiques a formulation in al-Mawaqif, clarifying that 'influence' here means 'bringing into existence'. He then provides two possible answers: (1) influence at the time of existence is acceptable if the existence obtained is the very existence resulting from that influence, not a prior one; (2) influence at the time of non-existence is also possible if the effect follows immediately, with no temporal gap. This refutes the objection that influence is impossible.

Key Terms
إيجاد
إعدام
علة
معلول
متأخر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that influence at existence is always tautological (making what already exists).
Correction: The author shows that if the existence obtained is precisely the one resulting from the influence, it is not tautological—the example of blackness illustrates this.

Checkpoint
What example does the author use to show that influence at existence is not tautological?
A) Whiteness in snow
B) Blackness in a black body
C) Heat in fire
D) Motion in a ball

Key Takeaway
Causal influence is possible either at the time of existence (as simultaneous creation) or at non-existence (as immediate succession), without contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the fact that every effect in your life is either created simultaneously with its cause or follows instantaneously, does it make you feel Allah's direct involvement in every moment? How can you cultivate that awareness throughout your day?
?
This lesson argues that causal influence at non-existence does not combine opposites because the effect follows immediately after the cause. How does this truth affect your understanding of Allah's power in bringing things from nothingness? Are you living as if you truly believe He can create change in an instant?
?
If you truly internalize that Allah's influence is not limited by the need for a prior existence or a gap in time, how might that change your trust in His ability to answer your prayers without delay? What is one specific area of your life where you need to act on that trust today?

The Objection from Equal Alternatives and Its Refutation
The author refutes the argument that choice between equals disproves the need for a cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the objection that choice between two equal alternatives disproves the need for a cause.

Core Idea
The will itself is the preponderator that resolves equal alternatives.

This lesson tackles a classic objection against the principle of causality. Critics point to everyday choices between equal options as evidence that things can happen without a cause. The author responds by distinguishing between the absence of an external preponderator and the presence of an internal cause—the will.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Begin by reading the passage where the objection is presented: if everything needs a cause, then choices between equals would be impossible, but we observe them, so the premise is false.
The objection uses examples of a thirsty person, hungry person, and person fleeing a lion.
2
Understand the author's answer
The author concedes the absence of an external preponderator but argues that the choice is not uncaused; it is a preponderance by the chooser, which is not the point of dispute.
The author distinguishes between a contingent occurring without any cause and a free agent choosing without an external cause.
3
Examine the counter-objection and reply
The objector then says that the choice itself is a contingent event that occurred without a cause. The author replies that it occurred by the will, which naturally preponderates and specifies.
The will is the internal cause that makes one option preferred over another.
4
Reflect on the role of the will
Consider how the author's argument preserves causality by attributing choice to a caused cause (the will) rather than to no cause at all.
This refutation is key to the Ash'ari position on qadar and causality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أنه لو امتنع وقوع الممكن بلا مؤثر وترجحه بلا مرجح لما وقع. واللازم باطل بحكم الضرورة، في مثل العطشان يشرب أحد الماءين، والجائع يأكل أحد الرغيفين، والهارب من السبع يسلك أحد الطريقين مع فرض التساوي وعدم المرجح . والجواب : بعد تسليم عدم المرجح عند العقل أصلاً، أن هذا ليس من وقوع الممكن بلا سبب وترجح أحد طرفيه بلا مرجح، بل من ترجيح المختار أحد الأمرين المتساويين من غير مرجح ومخصص، وهو غير المتنازع . فإن قيل : هذا الاختيار والترجيح أمر ممكن وقع بلا سبب وفيه المطلوب. قلنا ممنوع بل إنما وقع بالإرادة التي من شأنها الترجيح والتخصيص
And among them is that if the occurrence of the contingent without a cause and its preponderance without a preponderator were impossible, it would not occur. But the necessary consequence is false by necessity, as in the case of the thirsty person drinking one of two waters, the hungry person eating one of two loaves, and the person fleeing from a lion taking one of two paths, assuming equality and absence of a preponderator. The answer: after conceding the absence of a preponderator for the intellect absolutely, this is not from the occurrence of the contingent without a cause and the preponderance of one of its sides without a preponderator, but rather from the preponderance of the chooser of one of two equal things without a preponderator and specificator, and this is not the point of dispute. For if it is said: this choice and preponderance is a contingent matter that occurred without a cause, and therein lies the required point. We say: it is denied; rather it occurred by the will, whose property is preponderance and specification.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the second objection against the necessity of a cause. The objectors argue that if everything that occurs needs a cause or preponderator, then actions like choosing between two equal alternatives would be impossible. But we observe such choices, so the premise is false. The author responds that the objector is conflating two issues. The contingent's occurrence without a cause is not the same as a free agent choosing between two equal options. In the latter case, the choice is not uncaused; it is caused by the will, which is a specific cause that can preponderate one option over another without an external preponderator. Thus, the objection fails.

Key Terms
مرجح
ترجيح
تساوي
اختيار
إرادة
تخصيص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Choice between two equal alternatives without an external preponderator is evidence that events can occur without any cause.
Correction: The author clarifies that such choices are not uncaused; they are caused by the will, which is a cause that preponderates by its nature.

Checkpoint
How does the author respond to the objection that choice between equals shows things can occur without a cause?
A) He admits that such choices are uncaused
B) He argues that the will itself is a cause that preponderates
C) He denies that such choices occur
D) He says it is an exception to the rule

Key Takeaway
The will (إرادة) is a cause that preponderates between equal alternatives, so such choices are not uncaused.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a decision between two seemingly equal options, do you sometimes hesitate or feel anxious? How does knowing that your own will is a sufficient cause for choice affect the way you approach such decisions? Will you now trust your will more confidently and make a choice without waiting for an external sign?
?
The author distinguishes between an event occurring without any cause and a choice caused by the will. Reflect on a time you attributed a decision to 'just going with the flow' or 'randomness'. Can you honestly admit that your will was the real cause? What would change if you always acknowledged your willing as the decisive factor?
?
This lesson teaches that the will naturally preponderates. Have you ever used the excuse 'I couldn't decide' to delay responsibility? In light of this truth, what is one area in your life where you need to stop hiding behind 'no preponderator' and simply exercise your will? Commit to one decision today that you have been avoiding.

The Objection from Non-Existence Not Needing a Cause
Third objection and start of its answer regarding non-existence and causality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that if existence requires a cause, so too does non-existence, and the author's reply based on non-existence being pure negation.

Core Idea
Non-existence is pure negation and cannot be an effect.

This passage presents the third objection against the principle that contingent existence requires a cause. The objector argues symmetrically: if existence needs a cause, non-existence must need one as well. The author begins his response by denying the necessary entailment, pointing out that non-existence is pure negation and thus not a suitable candidate for being an effect. The answer is cut off here, but the foundational rebuttal is established.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the objector's logic: existence and non-existence are equal in needing a cause, but non-existence is said to be pure negation, so it cannot be an effect, hence the original claim (that existence needs a cause) must be false.
2
Identify the author's response
The author begins by denying the 'entailment' (mulāzama). He says: even if non-existence cannot be an effect, that does not mean existence does not need a cause. The claim of equality (tasāwī) is the point of contention.
The answer is incomplete; the full argument continues on the next page.
3
Reflect on the key concept: pure negation
Consider why non-existence being 'pure negation' (nafy maḥḍ) makes it unsuitable as an effect. An effect must be a real entity; non-existence is nothing, so it cannot be produced.
This is a fundamental distinction in causality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أنه لو احتاج الممكن في وجوده إلى المؤثر، لاحتاج إليه في عـدمـه لتساويها واللازم باطل لأن العدم نفي محض لا يصلح أثراً . والجواب : أن العدم إن لم يصلح أثراً، منعنا الملازمة لجواز أن يتساوى
And among them is that if the contingent needed a cause for its existence, it would need it for its non-existence because they are equal, but the necessary consequence is false because non-existence is pure negation and is not suitable as an effect. The answer: that if non-existence is not suitable as an effect, we deny the entailment because it is possible that they are equal...
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage presents the third objection and the beginning of its answer. The objector argues that if existence requires a cause, then by symmetry non-existence should also require one, but non-existence is pure negation and cannot be an effect, so the original claim is false. The author begins his response by denying the entailment (ملازمة) between the two, because even if existence needs a cause, non-existence does not necessarily need one, since non-existence is not a real thing that can be an effect. The answer is cut off here, but the argument continues on the next page.

Key Terms
عدم
نفي محض
أثر
ملازمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If existence needs a cause, then by logical symmetry non-existence must also need a cause.
Correction: The author denies this symmetry. Non-existence is pure negation and not a real entity, so it cannot be an effect. The two cases are not equal in the relevant sense.

Checkpoint
What is the objector's claim in this passage?
A) That non-existence is a real effect
B) That if existence needs a cause, non-existence must also need a cause
C) That existence does not need a cause
D) That non-existence is impossible

Key Takeaway
The objection from symmetry fails because non-existence is pure negation and cannot be an effect; the entailment between existence and non-existence needing a cause is denied.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Think of a time when you demanded symmetry in your expectations of Allah's treatment—for example, expecting equal reward for small deeds and punishment for minor sins. Does this lesson's denial of symmetry between existence and non-existence help you see why such expectations might be misguided? What would it take for you to accept asymmetry in divine justice?
?
Non-existence is pure negation—it is not a positive reality that needs a cause. Reflect: are there 'negatives' in your own life (absences, failures, lack of faith) that you treat as positive forces needing elaborate explanations? How can this lesson free you to focus on the positive realities that truly need a cause, like seeking Allah's guidance for your existence?

The Meaning of Influence and Effect
Defines influence and clarifies its temporal relation to effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of influence (ta'thīr) in Islamic theology and the temporal relationship between cause and effect.

Core Idea
Influence brings the possible from non-existence to existence without temporal gap.

This lesson delves into a foundational concept in Islamic theology: how a cause influences its effect. The passage clarifies that influence occurs at the moment of non-existence, and the effect follows immediately without any intervening moment. Understanding this helps resolve common misconceptions about causality and divine action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation to get a sense of the argument.
Notice the example of blackness in a black body.
2
Identify the definition of influence
Find where the author defines what influence (ta'thīr) means, especially the final sentence about bringing the possible from non-existence to existence.
3
Understand the temporal sequence
The author states that the cause precedes the effect in time, and there is no moment between them. Reflect on why this matters for the concept of causation.
The impossibility of lagging (takhalluf) means no intervening moment.
4
Reflect on the example of blackness
Consider the example of blackness in a black body. How does this illustrate that the existence obtained through influence is simultaneous with the influence?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الموجود بالوجود الحاصل بهذا الإيجاد، فلا نسلم استحالته، القابل. فإن السواد قائم بالجسم الأسود بهذا السواد، وإن أريد بوجود آخر سابق فلا نسلم لزومه فإن الوجود الحاصل بالتأثير مقارن له. وقد نختار أن التأثير حال العدم، ولا جمع بين النقيضين، لأن الأثر عقيب التأثير، بناء على أن المؤثر سابق على الأثر بالزمان أيضاً، ومعنى امتناع التخلف أنه لا يتخللهما آن وكان هذا مراد من أجاب بأن وجود المؤثر يستتبع وجود الأثر، على معنى أن وجود الأثر يحصل عقيب وجود المؤثر بصفة المؤثرية، وهو معنى التأثير فيكون في أن عدم الأثر، ويكون معنى تأثيره في الممكن إخراجه من العدم إلى الوجود.
The existent by the existence obtained through this bringing-into-existence, so we do not accept its impossibility, the recipient. For blackness subsists in the black body by this blackness, and if another prior existence is intended, we do not accept its necessity, for the existence obtained through influence is concomitant with it. And we may choose that influence occurs at the state of non-existence, and there is no combination of contradictories, because the effect is after the influence, based on the fact that the cause is prior to the effect in time as well, and the meaning of the impossibility of lagging is that no moment intervenes between them, and this was the intent of those who answered that the existence of the cause entails the existence of the effect, meaning that the existence of the effect occurs after the existence of the cause in its state of being a cause, which is the meaning of influence; thus it is that non-existence of the effect, and the meaning of its influence on the possible is its bringing it from non-existence to existence.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage clarifies the meaning of 'influence' (ta'thīr) and the relationship between a cause and its effect. It begins by asserting that the existence that comes about through creation (ījād) is not impossible, using the example of blackness inhering in a black body by that very blackness. If one posits a separate prior existence, that is not necessary, since the existence produced by influence is simultaneous with the influence. The author then presents a view that influence can occur at the moment of non-existence without combining contradictories, because the effect follows the influence temporally—the cause precedes the effect in time. The impossibility of lagging means that no moment intervenes between them. This is the meaning intended by those who say that the cause's existence entails the effect's existence: the effect occurs after the cause exists in its role as cause. Thus, the effect's non-existence is removed, and the influence on the possible is bringing it from non-existence to existence.

الإيجاد
التأثير
الأثر
المؤثر
الممكن
العدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think influence requires the cause to be simultaneous with the effect.
Correction: The passage clarifies that influence occurs at the moment of non-existence and the effect follows temporally, with no intervening moment.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the meaning of 'influence' (ta'thīr) on the possible?
A) Causing the possible to persist in existence
B) Bringing the possible from non-existence to existence
C) Creating the possible's essence
D) Making the possible necessary

Key Takeaway
Influence is the act of bringing a possible being from non-existence to existence, with the effect occurring immediately after the cause's existence in its causative state, without any intervening moment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a success or a trial, do you instinctively attribute it to a secondary cause (your effort, someone's action) or do you see it as directly brought into existence by Allah at that very moment? What does this passage teach you about the immediacy of Allah's action? How can you train yourself to recognize that every effect follows its cause without any gap—meaning that Allah's power is continuously and directly bringing things into existence? Are you living with that awareness, or are you disconnected?
?
If influence is bringing something from non-existence to existence, and the effect comes after the cause without any intervening moment, then every moment you exist is a direct act of creation by Allah. How does that change the way you view your own existence and your dependence on Him? What would it mean for you to truly internalize that there is no time—no gap—between your need and His provision? Are you living as if you are self-sufficient, or do you constantly turn to Him in your need?
?
The passage emphasizes that the effect does not lag behind the cause; it follows immediately. In your spiritual life, do you act as if there is a gap between your intention and Allah's response? Do you doubt that when you sincerely turn to Him, the effect (guidance, forgiveness, help) comes without delay? How can you trust in the immediacy of His response to your du'a and actions? What would change if you truly believed that no moment intervenes between your cause (your turning to Him) and His effect (His response)?
