Refuting the Objection about Persistence and Need
Al-Taftazani refutes the objection about persistence and clarifies the meaning of need.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that if need is due to imkan or huduth, then things would need a cause in persistence, and how al-Taftazani answers it.

Core Idea
Persistence is just existence in a second moment; need means impossibility without a cause.

After establishing the correct view, al-Taftazani addresses a powerful objection: if the need for a cause is due to imkan or huduth, which are continuous, then the possible/originated would still need a cause when persisting, leading to absurdities like 'obtaining the obtained' or implying independence. He provides a nuanced answer clarifying the meaning of need and persistence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the objection: if the cause of need is imkan or huduth, then since these are constant, the thing would need a cause in persistence. That leads to two absurdities: either effect upon existence (tahsil al-hasil) or effect upon persistence (which is not the thing itself). Also, imkan would cause need in prior nonexistence.
Identify the two parts of the objection.
2
Understand the answer's key move
Al-Taftazani answers by redefining need: it means the thing's existence or non-existence depends on something such that it is impossible without it. Persistence (baqa') is just existence considered in relation to a second moment. So need in persistence is simply that the continued existence depends on the cause.
Notice the distinction between existence and persistence.
3
Apply the answer to the objection
Thus, the objection's 'tahsil al-hasil' is avoided because need in persistence is not for bringing into existence but for continuation. Also, the need in prior nonexistence is not a problem because need is only about the possibility of existence or non-existence, not about actual nonexistence.
Connect the answer to each part of the objection.
4
Reflect on the concept of baqa'
The passage ends by stating that baqa' is not a separate entity but existence taken with a temporal qualification. This is a key metaphysical point in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قد سبق أن الممكن محتاج إلى السبب. إلا أن ذلك عند الفلاسفة وبعض المتكلمين لإمكانه، وعند قدماء المتكلمين لحدوثه، وقيل لإمكانه مع الحدوث، وقيل بشرط الحدوث. احتجت الفلاسفة على دعواهم بأن العقل إذا لاحظ كون الشيء غير مقتضي الوجود أو العدم بالنظر إلى ذاته حكم بأن وجوده أو عدمه لا يكون إلا بسبب خارج وهو معنى الاحتياج، سواء لاحظ كونه مسبوقاً بالعدم أو لم يلاحظ. واحتجوا على إبطال مذهب المخالف بأن الحدوث وصف للوجود ومتأخر عنه لكونه عبارة عن مسبوقية الوجود بالعدم، والوجود متأخر عن تأثير المؤثر، وهو عن الاحتياج إليه، وهو عن علة الاحتياج وجزئها وشرطها، فلو كان الحدوث علة للاحتياج أو جزأها أو شرطها، لزم تأخر الشيء عن نفسه بمراتب. وعارضهم بعض المتكلمين، فقالوا: سبب الاحتياج هو الحدوث، لأن العقل إذا لاحظ كون الشيء مما يوجد بعد العدم، حكم باحتياجه إلى علة تخرجه من العدم إلى الوجود، وإن لم يلاحظ كونه غير ضروري الوجود والعدم. ولا يجوز أن يكون هو الإمكان، لأنه كيفية لنسبة الوجود إلى الماهية فيتأخر عن الوجود المتأخر عن التأثير المتأخر عن الاحتياج إلى المؤثر. والحق أن هذه العلة إنما هي بحسب العقل بمعنى أنه يلاحظ الإمكان أو الحدوث فيحكم بالاحتياج، كما يقال علة المحصول في الخير هو التحيز لا بحسب الخارج بأن يتحقق الإمكان أو الحدوث فيوجد الاحتياج. وبهذا يظهر أن كلام الفريقين في الإبطال مغالطة. وأما في الإثبات، فكلام المتأخرين أظهر، وبالقبول أجدر.

واعترض بأنه لو كان علة الاحتياج إلى المؤثر هو الإمكان أو الحدوث، وهما لازمان للممكن والحادث لزم احتياجهما حالة البقاء لدوام المعلول بدوام العلة، واللازم باطل لأن التأثير حينئذ إما في الوجود وقد حصل بمجرد وجود المؤثر فيلزم تحصيل الحاصل بحصول سابق، وإما في البقاء أو أمر آخر متجدد، وهو تأثير في غير الباقي، أعني الممكن والحادث فيلزم استغناؤهما عن المؤثر. وفي كون الإمكان علة الاحتياج فساد آخر، وهو احتياج الممكن إلى المؤثر حال عدمه السابق، مع أنه نفي محض أزلي لا يعقل له مؤثر. الجواب أن معنى احتياج الممكن أو الحادث إلى المؤثر، توقف حصول الوجود له أو العدم أو استمرارهما على تحقق أمر أو انتفائه، بمعنى امتناعه بدون ذلك، وهو معنى دوام الأثر بدوام المؤثر. وإذا تحققت فاستمرار الوجود، أعني البقاء، ليس إلا وجوداً مأخوذاً بالإضافة إلى الزمان الثاني، وصحة قولنا وجد فلم يبق ولم يستمر لا يدل إلا على مغايرة البقاء لمطلق الوجود ولا نزاع في ذلك.
It has already preceded that the possible [thing] is in need of the cause. Except that this, according to the philosophers and some theologians, is due to its possibility, and according to the early theologians, due to its origination, and it was said [it is] due to its possibility along with origination, and it was said conditioned by origination. The philosophers argued for their claim that the intellect, when it observes that a thing does not necessitate existence or nonexistence with respect to its essence, judges that its existence or nonexistence only occurs through an external cause, and that is the meaning of need, whether it observes that it is preceded by nonexistence or does not observe. And they argued for the invalidation of the opponent's view that origination is a description of existence and posterior to it, because it is an expression of the precedence of existence by nonexistence, and existence is posterior to the effect of the agent, and it [the effect] is posterior to the need for it [the agent], and it [the need] is posterior to the cause of need, its part, and its condition. So if origination were the cause of need, or its part, or its condition, it would entail the thing being posterior to itself by degrees. And some theologians opposed them, and they said: the cause of need is origination, because the intellect, when it observes that a thing is of the kind that comes into existence after nonexistence, judges its need for a cause that brings it out from nonexistence into existence, even if it does not observe that it is not necessary in existence and nonexistence. And it is not permissible that it be possibility, because it is a modality of the relation of existence to essence, and thus it is posterior to existence, which is posterior to the effect, which is posterior to the need for the agent. And the truth is that this cause is only according to the intellect, in the sense that it observes possibility or origination and judges the need, just as it is said: the cause of the product in kheir is determination [in space], not according to external [reality] such that possibility or origination are realized and then need comes to exist. Misconception: Persistence (baqa') is a separate attribute from existence that requires a fresh act of creation.

According to al-Taftazani's answer, what does the need of a thing for a cause in the state of persistence mean?
A) It means the thing requires a new act of creation every moment.
B) It means the continued existence of the thing is dependent on the cause.
C) It means the thing's persistence is a separate entity that needs a cause.
D) It means the need only applies at the moment of origination, not persistence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You exist at this very moment, but you were nothing before, and without Allah's constant preservation you would return to nothing. Have you ever truly felt this moment-by-moment dependence on your Creator? What would change in your heart if you lived with this awareness every second?
?
Al-Taftazani teaches that persistence is just existence in a second moment. Your life is a series of such moments. Do you take your continued existence for granted, as if it is automatic? ?

How often do you act as if your initial dependence on Allah is enough, forgetting that you need Him for every subsequent breath? What would it look like to live with a constant sense of need for Allah in every small and big thing?

The Cause of Need for an Effect and Its Refutation
Al-Taftazani refutes an objection about the need for an effect to persist.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Taftazani refutes the objection that the need for a cause would persist eternally if the cause is possibility or origination.

Core Idea
Persistence of an effect is just continued existence depending on the same cause.

Al-Taftazani has been discussing the need of possible beings for an effect (a cause). He now addresses an objection: if the cause of need is possibility or origination, then the need would persist forever, leading to absurdities. His answer clarifies that persistence is not a new existence but a continuation of the same existence, which still depends on the cause. This lesson unpacks that subtle but crucial argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the objection begins with 'و اعترض بأنه' and the answer with 'الجواب أن'.
2
Identify the two views on the cause of need
The passage first mentions that the cause of need could be determination (taḥayyuz) or origination (ḥudūth). Note how al-Taftazani dismisses the negation arguments of both groups as fallacious.
He then says the later scholars' affirmative view is more evident.
3
Understand the objection
The objection argues that if possibility or origination is the cause of need, then the need would persist because they are permanent attributes. This would lead to either a redundant effect (if the cause acts on existence already present) or a new effect on something not persistent.
Also, possibility would imply need before existence, which is absurd.
4
Grasp the answer
Al-Taftazani responds that 'need' means dependence of both existence and continuation on the cause. Continuation is not a separate existence but the same existence related to a later time.
The fact that we say 'it existed and did not persist' only shows that continuance is conceptually distinct from existence, not that it lacks dependence.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
See how the answer resolves the objection without needing a new cause for each moment. The same cause that brought the thing into existence also sustains it.
This is a key point in the Ashʿarī doctrine of continuous creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو الحدوث فيحكم بالاحتياج. كما يقال علة المحصول في الخير هو التحيز لا بحسب الخارج بأن يتحقق الإمكان أو الحدث فيوجد الاحتياج، وبهذا يظهر أن كلام الفريقين في الإبطال مغالطة. وأما في الإثبات، فكلام المتأخرين أظهر، وبالقبول أجدر . واعترض بأنه لو كان علة الاحتياج إلى المؤثر هو الإمكان أو الحدوث، وهما لازمان ،للممكن والحادث لزم احتياجهما حالة (۱) البقاء لدوام المعلول بدوام العلة واللازم باطل لأن التأثير حينئذ إما في الوجود وقد حصل بمجرد وجود المؤثر فيلزم تحصيل الحاصل بحصول سابق، وإما في البقاء أو أمر آخر متجدد، وهو تأثير في غير الباقي، أعني الممكن والحادث فيلزم استغناؤهما عن المؤثر، وفي كون الإمكان علة الاحتياج فساد آخر، وهـو احتياج الممكن إلى المؤثر حال عدمه السابق، مع أنه نفي محض أزلي لا يعقل له مؤثر . الجواب أن معنى احتياج الممكن أو الحادث إلى المؤثر، توقف ؛ حصول الوجود له أو العدم أو استمرارهما على تحقق أمر أو انتفائه، بمعنى امتناعه بدون ذلك، وهو معنى دوام الأثر بدوام المؤثر، وإذا تحققت فاستمرار الوجود. أعني البقاء، ليس إلا وجوداً مأخوذاً (۳) بالإضافة إلى الزمان الثاني، وصحة قولنا وجد فلم يبق ولم يستمر لا يدل إلا على مغايرة البقاء لمطلق الوجود ولا نزاع في ذلك .
Or [it is] origination (al-ḥudūth), so it judges [the need]. As it is said: the cause (ʿilla) of the product in good is determination (al-taḥayyuz) not according to the external, such that possibility (al-imkān) or origination is realized, so the need exists. By this it appears that the speech of the two groups in negation is a fallacy. As for affirmation, the speech of the later scholars is more evident and more worthy of acceptance. And an objection was made: if the cause of the need for an effect (al-muʾaththir) were possibility or origination, and they are necessary concomitants (lāzimān) of the possible (al-mumkin) and the originated (al-ḥādith), then their need would follow in the state of continuance (al-baqāʾ) because of the persistence of the effect by the persistence of the cause, and the necessary consequent is false because the effect (al-taʾthīr) then is either in existence (al-wujūd) and it has already occurred by the mere existence of the effect, so it necessitates the acquisition of the obtained by a prior acquisition, or it is in continuance or some other renewing matter, and that is an effect in something other than the persistent, namely the possible and the originated, so their independence from the effect would follow. And in [the claim] that possibility is the cause of need there is another corruption, which is the need of the possible for an effect in its previous state of non-existence, while it is pure eternal negation for which no effect can be conceived. The answer: the meaning of the need of the possible or originated for an effect is the dependence (tawaqquf) of the attainment of existence for it, or non-existence, or their continuation, upon the realization of something or its negation, in the sense of its impossibility without that. That is the meaning of the persistence of the effect by the persistence of the effect. And if you realize [this], then the continuation of existence, I mean continuance, is nothing but existence taken (maʾkhūdhan) in relation to the second time, and the correctness of our saying: 'It existed and did not continue and did not persist' indicates only the difference (mukhālafa) of continuance from absolute existence, and there is no dispute about that.
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage discusses the cause of the need of a possible or originated thing for an effect (a cause that brings it into existence). The author first mentions two alternative views: the cause of need is either determination (taḥayyuz) or origination (ḥudūth). He then states that the speech of the two groups (likely the Muʿtazila and Ashʿarīs?) in negation is fallacious, while in affirmation the later scholars' speech is better. Then an objection is presented: if the cause of need is possibility or origination, which are necessary concomitants, then the need would persist as long as the thing persists, because the effect (the cause's influence) would have to be either in existence (already obtained) or in continuance (which would imply a new effect, making the thing independent of the cause). Additionally, if possibility is the cause, the possible would need an effect even in its state of non-existence, which is absurd. The author responds by defining the need as the dependence of both existence and continuation on the cause. Continuation is not a new existence but the same existence related to a second time. The fact that we can say 'it existed and did not persist' only shows that continuance is distinct from absolute existence, but this does not contradict the need.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that persistence (baqāʾ) is a new state that requires a separate cause distinct from the original cause.
Correction: The author clarifies that persistence is not a new existence but the same existence in relation to a later time; it still depends on the same cause that brought it into being.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, what does the need of the possible or originated thing for an effect (muʾaththir) mean?
A) It depends on the cause only for its initial existence.
B) Its existence and persistence both depend on the cause.
C) It depends on the cause only for its persistence.
D) It does not need a cause for persistence.

Key Takeaway
Persistence of a possible thing is not a separate existence but a continuation of the same existence, and it depends on the same cause that originated it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live today as if your next breath is a given, or do you truly feel that each moment of your existence is sustained by the same Cause that brought you into being? What would change if you internalized that your persistence is nothing but the same existence held by God at every instant?
?
This lesson says that continuance is not a separate reality but the same existence linked to a later time. If your own existence is just a continuous gift, not a self-sustained state, then how does that confront your pride or your sense of independence? Will you pause right now to acknowledge that you depend on God not only for your first moment but for your continued being?
?
The objection feared redundancy or independence in causation. But the answer says the Cause remains the same. In your life, do you sometimes feel that God's role is only in the past (creation) and now you are autonomous? What would it mean to truly believe that He is the constant Preserver, not just the Originator?

First Objection Against Inherent Preponderance and Its Refutation
First objection that inherent preponderance leads to contradiction and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first objection raised by the majority against inherent preponderance and the author's refutation, including the logical dilemma and the distinction between preponderance and necessity.

Core Idea
Inherent preponderance does not imply necessity; it is a preponderance short of necessity.

The majority of theologians argued that inherent preponderance in a possible leads to contradictions. Their first objection presents a dilemma: either the preponderant side becomes necessary, or the possible side occurs without cause. In response, the author clarifies that the preponderance at issue is not absolute but a relative preference that does not reach the level of necessity. This passage sharpens the concept of inherent preponderance.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context of the objection
Recognize that the majority are arguing against the possibility of inherent preponderance in a possible entity. Why does this matter? If a possible has an inherent leaning, it might seem to imply necessity.
This objection is one of several arguments against inherent preponderance.
2
Follow the dilemma presented
The objection sets up two horns: either the other side becomes impossible (making the first necessary) or if still possible, its occurrence requires a cause, leading to a contradiction.
Notice the explicit 'إما...أو' structure in the Arabic.
3
Identify the refutation's key move
The answer denies that preponderance reaches the point of necessity. It is a preponderance short of necessity, so the horns do not apply.
The refutation hinges on the distinction between preponderance and absolute necessity.
4
Connect to broader doctrine
How does this refutation preserve the possibility of inherent preponderance without collapsing into necessitarianism?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستدل الجمهور على امتناعه بوجوه : الأول : أنه لو كان أحد الطرفين أولى بالممكن نظر إلى ذاته، فمع تلك الأولوية، إما أن يمتنع وقوع الطرف الآخر فيكون الطرف الأولى واجباً لذات الممكن فلا يكون ممكناً، بل واجباً أو ممتنعاً هذا خلف وإنما يمكن، وحينئذ فوقوعه إما أن يكون بلا سبب يرجحه، فيلزم ترجيح المرجوح أعني الطرف الغير الأولى، أو يكون بسبب بغير رجحانه فيكون وقوع الطرف الأولى متوقفاً على عدم ذلك السبب، فلا يكون أولى بالنظر إلى ذات الممكن بل مع عدم ذلك السبب هذا خلف. والجواب : أنه لا يلزم من توقف الوقوع على أمر توقف الأولوية عليه، حتى يلزم كونها غير ذاتية، وذلك لأن التقدير أن المراد بها رجحان ما لا إلى حد الوجوب.
And the majority argued for its impossibility with arguments: The first: That if one of the two sides is preponderant over the possible with respect to its essence, then with that preponderance, either the occurrence of the other side becomes impossible, so the preponderant side becomes necessary by the essence of the possible, so it would not be possible, but rather necessary or impossible—this is a contradiction—but rather it is possible. Then its occurrence is either without a cause that preponderates it, resulting in the preponderance of the less likely—meaning the non-preponderant side—or it is due to a cause without its preponderance, so the occurrence of the preponderant side depends on the absence of that cause, so it is not preponderant with respect to the essence of the possible but rather with the absence of that cause—this is a contradiction. And the answer: That it does not follow from the dependence of occurrence on something that the preponderance depends on it, so that it would be non-essential; that is because the supposition is that what is meant by it is a preponderance that does not reach the point of necessity.
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage presents the first objection from the majority against the idea that a possible can have an inherent preponderance and the author's refutation. The objection argues by dilemma: if one side is inherently preponderant, then either the other side is impossible (making the first necessary) or it is still possible but occurs without a preponderant cause or with a non-preponderant cause, leading to contradiction. The answer denies that the preponderance is to the point of necessity; it is a preponderance short of necessity, so the objection's conclusion does not follow. The author clarifies that the preponderance in question is not absolute necessity but a relative preponderance.

Key Terms
أولى
وجوب
إمكان
ترجيح المرجوح
خلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any preponderance in a possible entity implies that the preponderant side is necessary.
Correction: The author clarifies that inherent preponderance is a relative preference that does not reach the point of necessity (رجحان ما لا إلى حد الوجوب). Thus, it does not make the preponderant side necessary.

Checkpoint
What is the first objection's main argument against inherent preponderance?
A) It leads to the preponderant side becoming necessary.
B) It leads to the preponderant side being impossible.
C) It leads to either the preponderant side becoming necessary or to a contradiction in the possible.
D) It leads to the possibility of the less likely side occurring.

Key Takeaway
The first objection fails because inherent preponderance is a relative preference, not an absolute necessitation, so the dilemma does not apply.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever treat your own preferences as if they were absolute necessities, forgetting that they are mere preponderances that could be otherwise? How does this lesson challenge your attitude toward your own inclinations?

The objection assumes that preponderance must lead to impossibility. In your life, have you ever assumed that because you feel strongly about something, its opposite is unthinkable? How does the author's refutation free you from such absolutism?

Third Objection: The Dilemma of Essential Preponderance and Its Refutation
Third objection: essential preponderance leads to a dilemma, and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third objection to essential preponderance and how the author refutes it by distinguishing inherent preponderance from actual necessity.

Core Idea
Essential preponderance does not necessitate actual occurrence; external causes can override without removing it.

This lesson presents the third objection against essential preponderance (al-ula al-dhatiyya) and its refutation. The objection attempts to force a contradiction: if preponderance is essential, it must be either removable or not, each leading to a problem. The response clarifies that essential preponderance is not to the point of necessity and remains intact even when external factors determine actual occurrence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to grasp the overall argument. Notice the objection's two horns and the author's answer.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the structure
Identify the objection (with two conditional statements) and the answer introduced by 'Wa al-jawab'.
The objection uses 'fa-in amkana... wa in lam yumkin'.
3
Understand the two horns
First horn: if removable, preponderance depends on a cause and is not essential. Second horn: if not removable, the preponderant side becomes necessary, contradicting possibility.
Each horn is designed to show a contradiction.
4
Grasp the refutation
The answer denies that the impossibility of removal entails occurrence or necessity. It introduces the idea of essential entailment not reaching the point of wajub, and external causes determining actuality.
Key phrase: 'la yalzam min imtina' al-zawal... wuqu'ahu'.
5
Reflect on the core idea
Essential preponderance is a real but limited property; it does not force actual existence. External causes complete the determination.
This preserves both essential preponderance and contingency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : أنه لو كان أحد الطرفين أولى لذات الممكن، فإما أن يمكن زوال تلك الأولوية بسبب أو لا. فإن أمكن لم تكن الأولوية ذاتية لتوقفها على ذلك السبب، ولأن ما بالذات لا يزول بالغير، وإن لم يمكن كان الطرف الأولى ضروريا بذات الممكن، فلم يكن الممكن ممكناً، بل واجباً إن كان هو الوجود، وممتنعاً إن كان هو العدم. والجواب : أنه لا يلزم من امتناع زوال أولوية الوجود أو العدم بالمعنى الذي ذكرنا وقوعه، فضلاً عن كونه ضرورياً ليلزم وجوب الممكن أو امتناعه، وذلك لأنه يجوز أن يقتضي ذات الممكن الموجود اقتضاء ما لا إلى حد الوجوب والوقوع، ويقع العدم باقتضاء أسباب خارجية، تنتهي إلى حد الوجوب والوقوع أو بالعكس، وتكون الأولوية الذاتية بحالها باقية غير زائلة.
The third: That if one of the two sides is preponderant by the essence of the possible, then either the removal of that preponderance is possible due to a cause or not. If possible, then the preponderance would not be essential because it depends on that cause, and because what is essential does not cease by another. If not possible, then the preponderant side would be necessary by the essence of the possible, so the possible would not be possible, but rather necessary if it is existence, and impossible if it is non-existence. And the answer: That the impossibility of the removal of the preponderance of existence or non-existence in the sense we mentioned does not entail its occurrence, let alone it being necessary so as to necessitate the necessity or impossibility of the possible; that is because it is permissible that the essence of the possible existence entails an entailment not to the point of necessity and occurrence, and non-existence occurs by the entailment of external causes that end at the point of necessity and occurrence, or vice versa, and the essential preponderance remains as it is, not ceasing.
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage presents the third objection and its refutation. The objection poses a dilemma: if the preponderance is essential, it must be either removable or not; if removable, it depends on a cause and is not essential; if not removable, the side becomes necessary, contradicting possibility. The answer clarifies that the preponderance in question is not to the point of necessity (law wajib). Even if it cannot be removed, that does not mean the side necessarily occurs, because external causes can override without removing the inherent preponderance. The inherent preponderance remains as it is, but actual occurrence depends on external factors reaching necessity.

Key Terms
أولوية ذاتية (essential preponderance)
زوال (removal)
ضروري (necessary)
اقتضاء أسباب خارجية (entailment of external causes)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If essential preponderance cannot be removed, then the preponderant side must actually occur and be necessary.
Correction: The author shows that impossibility of removal does not entail occurrence; essential preponderance is an entailment not reaching necessity, and external causes are needed for actuality.

Checkpoint
What does the answer to the third objection say about the essential preponderance when external causes are present?
A) It is negated by external causes.
B) It remains as it is and does not cease.
C) It becomes necessary.
D) It disappears.

Key Takeaway
Essential preponderance is a real inherent property that does not necessitate actual existence; external causes determine actuality while the preponderance remains unchanged.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Consider a persistent sin or virtue in your life. Is your response to it fatalistic—'I cannot change because this is who I am'—or do you actively seek the 'external causes' of tawfiq, effort, and environment to override your tendencies? Which reality are you ignoring?
?
The essential preponderance remains unchanged even when external causes bring about the opposite. In your spiritual journey, what 'essential preponderance' (e.g., love of comfort, pride, or desire for Allah) do you perceive that persists despite your actions? Will you accept it as a permanent inclination and still work to let external causes (e.g., worship, sincere supplication) actualize the good?

The Necessity of Preponderance Reaching Necessity for Actual Occurrence
Concluding argument that preponderance must reach necessity for a possible to occur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why mere preponderance is insufficient for the occurrence of a possible, and how necessity through choice reconciles with free will.

Core Idea
Occurrence requires necessity, not just preference; necessity through choice preserves free will.

This passage presents the concluding argument that for any contingent thing to come into existence, mere preponderance (al-awlawiyyah) is not enough; it must reach the level of necessity (al-wujub). The author explains that if only preponderance existed, both sides could be possible, leading to a preponderance without a preponderant, which is impossible. He also clarifies that this necessity does not negate free choice because it is a necessity that arises through the agent's choice as part of the complete cause.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem of equality
Consider why if both occurrence and non-occurrence were equally possible, a preponderance without a preponderant would result, which is impossible.
This is the core logical problem that drives the need for necessity.
2
Grasp the conclusion: preponderance must become necessity
The author states that mere preponderance is not sufficient; it must reach the point of necessity, meaning the opposite becomes impossible by another.
Necessity here is conditioned necessity (wujub bil-ghayr).
3
Consider the intellect's role in priority
Note that the 'prior existence' mentioned is not temporal but intellectual; the intellect judges that nothing exists unless it becomes necessary.
4
Address the misconception about free will
Understand how necessity through choice does not negate free will—choice is part of the complete cause, making the act necessary but chosen.
This reconciles determinism with human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : إذ لا بد من ذلك لأن الوقوع تارة واللاوقوع أخرى من استواء الحالين ترجح بلا مرجع، فالممكن ما لم يجب صدوره لم يوجد، وعين الوجود امتنع عدمه، فوجوده محفوف بوجودين سابق ولاحق، وليس معنى السبق الاحتياج في التحقق أو التعقل بل في اعتبار العقل عند ملاحظة هذه المعاني. بمعنى أنه يحكم بأنه لم يوجد ما لم يجب. وهذا الوجوب لا ينافي الاختيار لكونه بالاختيار الذي هو من تمام العلة. أنه لا يكفي في الوقوع مجرد الأولوية، بل لا بد من انتهائها إلى حد يعني الوجوب، بأن يصير الطرف الآخر ممتنعاً بالغير، إذ لو جاز وقوعه أيضاً، لكان وقوع الطرف الأول تارة، ولا وقوعه أخرى مع استواء الحالين، حيث لم يوجد إلا مجرد الأولوية ترجحاً بلا مرجح. فالممكن بحسب صدوره عن العلة،
He said: For it is necessary that because occurrence sometimes and non-occurrence other times from the equality of the two states would be a preponderance without a preponderant, so the possible, as long as its emanation is not necessary, does not exist, and the very existence of existence is the impossibility of its non-existence, so its existence is surrounded by two existences—a prior and a posterior—and the meaning of priority is not need in actualization or conceptualization, but rather in the consideration of the intellect when observing these meanings. Meaning that it judges that nothing exists unless it becomes necessary. And this necessity does not contradict free choice because it is through choice which is part of the complete cause. That mere preponderance is not sufficient for occurrence; rather, it must end at the point of necessity—meaning that the other side becomes impossible by another—for if its occurrence were also possible, then the occurrence of the first side would sometimes be and sometimes not be, with the two states being equal, since there is only mere preponderance, which would be a preponderance without a preponderant. So the possible in terms of its emanation from the cause...
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This is the author's concluding argument. He explains that for a possible to actually occur, mere preponderance (al-awlawiyyah) is insufficient; the preponderance must reach the point of necessity (al-wujub). If only preponderance existed without necessity, the opposite could also occur, leading to randomness without a preponderant, which is impossible. Therefore, actual existence requires that the non-occurrence becomes impossible due to an external cause. This necessity does not negate free will because it is a necessity through choice—choice is part of the complete cause. The author also discusses the intellectual consideration of priority.

Key Terms
وجوب (necessity)
أولوية (preponderance)
ترجح بلا مرجح (preponderance without a preponderant)
اختيار (free choice)
علة تامة (complete cause)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Necessity in kalam always negates free will.
Correction: The author explains that this necessity is 'through choice' (bil-ikhtiyar) and is part of the complete cause, thus it does not negate free will.

Checkpoint
What is required for the actual occurrence of a possible according to the concluding argument?
A) Mere preponderance.
B) The preponderance must reach the point of necessity.
C) The preponderance must be essential.
D) The preponderance must be by choice.

Key Takeaway
Actual occurrence of a possible requires that its preponderance reaches the point of necessity, but this necessity is compatible with free will because it is a necessity through choice.

Essential Priority and the Necessity of Existence
Objection and answer on the necessity of the possible's priority to existence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection against essential priority of possibles is answered and why mere priority must reach the limit of necessity for actual existence.

Core Idea
Essential priority alone cannot cause existence; it must reach the limit of necessity.

This lesson presents a key objection in Islamic theology: if a possible being has an essential priority towards existence, wouldn't that make it necessary? The answer clarifies that essential priority is not sufficient and that external causes bring it to necessity, preserving both possibility and free choice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection: if the possible has an essential priority towards existence or non-existence, it would be either necessary or impossible, negating its possibility.
This objection challenges the concept of essential priority.
2
Grasp the answer
The answer distinguishes between essential priority and actual necessity. The possible's essence may necessitate something short of necessity; actual existence depends on external causes that bring it to the limit of necessity.
The essential priority remains unchanged but does not force occurrence.
3
Examine the supporting argument
The text argues that without necessity, occurrence would involve preponderance without a preponderator, which is impossible. So the possible must have a cause that necessitates its existence at the time of its actuality.
This is the classical principle of 'tarjih bila murajjih'.
4
Note compatibility with choice
This necessity does not contradict free choice because it is 'by choice' as part of the complete cause. The necessity is not coercive but stems from the free agent's choice.
5
Confirm the conclusion
Mere essential priority is insufficient; it must reach the stage where the opposite becomes impossible by another cause. This avoids the problem of preponderance without a preponderator.
The priority is like an inclination that needs external completion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأولى ضرورية للذات الممكن، فلم يكن الممكن ممكناً، بل واجباً إن كان هو الوجود، وممتنعاً إن كان هو العدم.
والجواب: أنه لا يلزم من امتناع زوال أولوية الوجود أو العدم بالمعنى الذي ذكرنا وقوعه، فضلاً عن كونه ضرورياً ليلزم وجوب الممكن أو امتناعه، وذلك لأنه يجوز أن يقتضي ذات الممكن الموجود اقتضاء ما لا إلى حد الوجوب والوقوع، ويقع العدم باقتضاء أسباب خارجية، تنتهي إلى حد الوجوب والوقوع أو بالعكس، وتكون الأولوية الذاتية بحالها باقية غير زائلة.
قال: إذ لا بد من ذلك لأن الوقوع تارة واللاوقوع أخرى من استواء الحالين ترجح بلا مرجح، فالممكن ما لم يجب صدوره لم يوجد، وعين الوجود امتنع عدمه، فوجوده محفوف بوجودين سابق ولاحق، وليس معنى السبق الاحتياج في التحقق أو التعقل بل في اعتبار العقل عند ملاحظة هذه المعاني. بمعنى أنه يحكم بأنه لم يوجد ما لم يجب.
وهذا الوجوب لا ينافي الاختيار لكونه بالاختيار الذي هو من تمام العلة.
أنه لا يكفي في الوقوع مجرد الأولوية، بل لا بد من انتهائها إلى حد يعني الوجوب، بأن يصير الطرف الآخر ممتنعاً بالغير، إذ لو جاز وقوعه أيضاً، لكان وقوع الطرف الأول تارة، ولا وقوعه أخرى مع استواء الحالين، حيث لم يوجد إلا مجرد الأولوية ترجحاً بلا مرجح.
The first priority is necessary for the essence of the possible, so the possible would not be possible, but rather necessary if it is existence, and impossible if it is non-existence. The answer: It does not follow from the impossibility of the removal of the priority of existence or non-existence in the sense we mentioned its occurrence, let alone its being necessary, so that the necessity or impossibility of the possible would follow. That is because it is permissible that the essence of the existing possible necessitates a necessitation that does not reach the limit of necessity and occurrence, and non-existence occurs by the necessitation of external causes that terminate at the limit of necessity and occurrence, or the opposite, and the essential priority remains as it is, not removed. He said: Indeed, this is necessary because occurrence at one time and non-occurrence at another, from the equality of the two states, would be a preponderance without a preponderator. So the possible, as long as its emanation is not necessary, does not exist, and when it exists, its non-existence becomes impossible. So its existence is surrounded by two existences: a prior and a posterior. The meaning of priority is not need in actualization or intellection, but rather in the consideration of the intellect when observing these meanings. Meaning that it judges that what must not [exist] does not exist. This necessity does not contradict choice because it is by choice, which is part of the complete cause. That mere priority is not sufficient for occurrence, rather it must reach the limit meaning necessity, such that the other side becomes impossible by another. For if its occurrence were also permissible, then the occurrence of the first side at one time and its non-occurrence at another, with the two states being equal, would be a preponderance without a preponderator.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer regarding the concept of essential priority (al-uwla al-dhatiyya) in the possible (al-mumkin). The objector argues that if the possible has an essential priority towards existence or non-existence, then it would actually be necessary (wajib) if the priority is to existence, or impossible (mumtani') if to non-existence, thus negating its possibility. The answer denies this entailment. It explains that the removal of such priority does not necessitate occurrence; rather, the essence of the possible may necessitate something short of absolute necessity, and actual existence or non-existence is determined by external causes that bring it to the point of necessity. The essential priority remains unchanged but does not force occurrence. The commentator then quotes the base text (قال) which argues that without necessity, occurrence and non-occurrence would be arbitrary (tarjih bila murajjih), so the possible must have a cause that necessitates its existence. This necessity, however, is compatible with free choice (ikhtiyar) because it is 'by choice' as part of the complete cause. Finally, the passage emphasizes that mere priority is insufficient; the priority must reach the level of necessity (wujub) by making the opposite side impossible by another cause, otherwise the problem of preponderance without a preponderator arises.

Key Terms
أولوية
واجب
ممتنع
ترجح بلا مرجح
اختيار
علة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mere essential priority is sufficient for actual existence.
Correction: Essential priority must be completed by external causes to reach the limit of necessity, otherwise the opposite remains possible and preponderance without a preponderator occurs.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for the actual occurrence (wuqu') of a possible being?
A) Mere essential priority towards existence
B) The priority must reach the limit of necessity, making the opposite impossible by another cause
C) The absence of any external causes
D) The possible must be necessary by itself

Key Takeaway
Essential priority alone cannot cause existence; it must be completed by external causes to reach the limit of necessity, preserving possibility and free choice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel naturally inclined towards something good, do you rely on that inclination alone, or do you actively seek the external means—like supplication, effort, and turning to Allah—to bring it about? Where might you be trusting mere 'priority' instead of seeking the complete cause?
?
The lesson shows that even your most sincere intentions remain merely potential until Allah brings them into actuality through His decree. Are you truly patient with outcomes that don't match your priorities, or do you become frustrated, forgetting that only when Allah necessitates something does it occur?
?
Your choices are real, yet they are encompassed by Allah's complete causation. Do you live with the awe of this mystery—that you are responsible and yet utterly dependent—or do you unconsciously lean towards denying either your responsibility or His all-encompassing will? Which subtle imbalance do you need to correct today?
